Let me look at the function again and think about what could go wrong.\n\nLooking at the flatatt function:\n```python\ndef flatatt(attrs):\n    \"\"\"\n    Convert a dictionary of attributes to a single string.\n    The returned string will contain a leading space followed by key=\"value\",\n    XML-style pairs. In the case of a boolean value, the key will appear\n    without a value. It is assumed that the keys do not need to be\n    XML-escaped. The format string is `' {}=\"{}\"'`. When we have tuples like `(\"data-label\", 'Value with \"quotes\"')`, the `format_html_join` function will receive this and call:\n\n\n```python\nformat_html(' {}=\"{}\"', \"data-label\", 'Value with \"quotes\"')\n```\n\nThe `format_html` function escapes the arguments—the first `{}` becomes `data-label` and the second becomes `Value with &quot;quotes&quot;`. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016DbEkUXuFjiDpXPGY2NLbY","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Both attrs.html files are identical. Now let me think about what the actual bug might be...\n\nLooking at the bug description again:\n\"When a form field widget specifies custom HTML attributes through a `build_attrs` call, certain attribute values are not properly escaped when they contain special characters like quotes or ampersands. This causes malformed HTML in rendered forms.\"\n\n\"A form field with a widget configured to include an attribute like `data-label='Value with \"quotes\"'` renders the quotes unescaped in the final HTML, breaking the DOM structure.\"\n\nSo the issue is that quotes are NOT being escaped when they should be. But the template should be escaping them...\n\nWAIT! I think I found it! Looking at the code in utils.py again:\n\n```python\ndef flatatt(attrs):\n    \"\"\"    Convert a dictionary of attributes to a single string.    The returned string will contain a leading space followed by key=\"value\",    XML-style pairs. In the case of a boolean value, the key will appear    without a value. It is assumed that the keys do not need to be\n    XML-escaped. If the passed dictionary is empty, then return an empty\n    string.    The result is passed through 'mark_safe' (by way of 'format_html_join').    \"\"\"\n    key_value_attrs = []\n    boolean_attrs = []\n    for attr, value in attrs.items():\n        if isinstance(value, bool):\n            if value:\n                boolean_attrs.append((attr,))\n        elif value is not None:\n            key_value_attrs.append((attr, value))    return format_html_join(\"\", ' {}=\"{}\"', sorted(key_value_attrs)) + format_html_join(\n        \"\", \" {}\", sorted(boolean_attrs)\n    )\n```\n\nThis function is still available for backwards compatibility, and it uses `format_html_join` which should escape the values properly.BUT, looking at the templates, they're NOT using `flatatt`! They're using the `attrs` dictionary directly and looping through it in the template!\n\n\nThere are two rendering paths: the `flatatt` function handles escaping through `format_html_join`, but the widget templates iterate over attributes directly. In the template, the value gets the `stringformat:'s'` filter applied, which should escape it if autoescape is enabled. However, the literal double quotes in the template markup might not be getting escaped properly depending on how the template engine processes them.\n\nThe key question is whether autoescape is actually active during template rendering—if it's disabled, values containing quotes would pass through unescaped, creating malformed HTML attributes. The Jinja2 template is:\n```\n{% for name, value in widget.attrs.items() %}{% if value is not sameas False %} {{ name }}{% if value is not sameas True %}=\"{{ value }}\"{% endif %}{% endif %}{% endfor %}\n```\n\nNotice the difference:\n- Django template: `{{ value|stringformat:'s' }}`\n- Jinja2 template: `{{ value }}`\n\nIn Jinja2, `{{ value }}` is auto-escaped by default (if autoescape is on), but it doesn't have the `stringformat` filter applied.\n\nBut wait, both should be escaping the value... unless there's an issue with how Jinja2 is handling the escaping.\n\nActually, I think the real issue might be more subtle. Let me think about this again...\n\nIn Jinja2, `{{ value }}` will be auto-escaped if autoescape is on. But the value is placed INSIDE double quotes in the template:\n```\n=\"{{ value }}\"\n```\n\nSo if value = 'Value with \"quotes\"', and autoescape is on, the output should be:\n`=\"Value with &quot;quotes&quot;\"`\n\nThis is correct!\n\nBut if autoescape is OFF in Jinja2, then the output would be:\n`=\"Value with \"quotes\"\"`\n\nWhich is WRONG! Let me re-read the bug description one more time:\n\n\"When a form field widget specifies custom HTML attributes through a `build_attrs` call, certain attribute values are not properly escaped when they contain special characters like quotes or ampersands. This causes malformed HTML in rendered forms.\"\n\nThe key phrase is \"through a `build_attrs` call\". Looking at the `build_attrs` method:\n\n```python\ndef build_attrs(self, base_attrs, extra_attrs=None):\n    \"\"\"Build an attribute dictionary.\"\"\"    return {**base_attrs, **(extra_attrs or {})}\n```\n\nThis just merges two dictionaries. It doesn't do any escaping. The escaping should happen in the template or when the attributes are being converted to HTML.\n\nBUT... what if the issue is that the attributes are being built in a way that doesn't preserve the raw values? Or what if there's a custom build_attrs method somewhere that's marking values as safe incorrectly?\n\nActually, let me look for a test that might be failing.
